<div class="container-fluid main-container">




<div id="practicle-machine-learning-course-project-writeup" class="section level2">
<h2>Practicle Machine Learning (Course Project Writeup)</h2>
<div id="goal" class="section level3">
<h3>Goal:</h3>
<p>The goal of your project is to predict the Classe Variable in the 
train dataset and implement the learned algorithm on the test dataset.</p>
</div>
<div id="the-approach" class="section level3">
<h3>The Approach:</h3>
<p>My Approach to the problem is very simple. First we will get rid of 
the variables having high missing values. After making sure that, now we
 have variables which do not have any missing values we will look for 
variables with very high correlation, because these highly correlated 
varibles can lead to multicollinearity which can increase miss 
classification error rate. Now as of now we have only 32 Variables that 
can used for prediction.</p>
<p>The next big quest is choosing the right algorithm which learns from 
the data to its best. Without much effort and extensively exploring the 
forums I found out that randomForest will be the best choice for the 
data, which uses the bragging method that is a high variance, low bias 
technique.</p>
<p>The learned algorithm from this data is then used to predict the test data.</p>
<p>** Note: I first took the approach of PCA but find it of no use. - 
Please create “D:\github\practicle_machine_learning\” directory in your 
D: drive - Please create “submission files” folder with the above 
diretory to store output ### Taking you along with the code</p>
<div id="importing-the-train-and-test-dataset-into-the-r" class="section level4">
<h4>Importing the train and test dataset into the R</h4>
<pre><code>## Warning: package 'caret' was built under R version 3.0.3</code></pre>
<pre><code>## Loading required package: lattice</code></pre>
<pre><code>## Warning: package 'lattice' was built under R version 3.0.3</code></pre>
<pre><code>## Loading required package: ggplot2</code></pre>
<pre><code>## Warning: package 'ggplot2' was built under R version 3.0.3
## Warning: package 'reshape' was built under R version 3.0.3
## Warning: package 'corrplot' was built under R version 3.0.3
## Warning: package 'AppliedPredictiveModeling' was built under R version 3.0.3</code></pre>
<pre><code>## randomForest 4.6-7
## Type rfNews() to see new features/changes/bug fixes.</code></pre>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">file.loc</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="string">"D:\\github\\practicle_machine_learning\\"</span>
<span class="identifier">setwd</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">paste0</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">file.loc</span>,<span class="string">"submission files"</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">)</span>
<span class="identifier">train</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">read.csv</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">paste0</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">file.loc</span>,<span class="string">"pml-training.csv"</span><span class="paren">)</span>,<span class="identifier">stringsAsFactor</span><span class="operator">=</span><span class="literal">FALSE</span>,<span class="identifier">skip</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="number">0</span>,<span class="identifier">fill</span><span class="operator">=</span><span class="literal">NA</span>,<span class="identifier">comment.char</span><span class="operator">=</span><span class="string">"#"</span><span class="paren">)</span>
<span class="identifier">test</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">read.csv</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">paste0</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">file.loc</span>,<span class="string">"pml-testing.csv"</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">)</span></code></pre>
</div>
<div id="removing-missing-data-variables" class="section level4">
<h4>Removing Missing data Variables:</h4>
<p>The train dataset consist of 160 variables and 19622 observations from which we have to learn.</p>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">length</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">names</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">train</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">)</span>  <span class="comment"># No.. of Varaibles</span></code></pre>
<pre><code>## [1] 160</code></pre>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">nrow</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">train</span><span class="paren">)</span>           <span class="comment"># No. of Observations </span></code></pre>
<pre><code>## [1] 19622</code></pre>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">var</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">names</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">train</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">[</span><span class="identifier">apply</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">train</span>,<span class="number">2</span>,<span class="keyword">function</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">x</span><span class="paren">)</span> <span class="identifier">table</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">is.na</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">x</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">[</span><span class="number">1</span><span class="paren">]</span><span class="operator">==</span><span class="number">19622</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">]</span>   
<span class="identifier">train2</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">train</span><span class="paren">[</span>,<span class="identifier">var</span><span class="paren">]</span>
<span class="identifier">test2</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">test</span><span class="paren">[</span>,<span class="identifier">var</span><span class="paren">[</span><span class="operator">-</span><span class="identifier">length</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">var</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">]</span><span class="paren">]</span></code></pre>
<p>Now, when we see the variables we still have some variables with “” <space>
 as value. Luckly we have a pattern of missing value within variables. 
Further we reduced our variables and kept only the numeric variables 
giving HAR information.</space></p>
<p>*Note : There is no need of creating the data frame again and again. I
 have created this only to bring clear picture for my approach.</p>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">var2</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">melt</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">apply</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">train2</span>,<span class="number">2</span>,<span class="keyword">function</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">x</span><span class="paren">)</span> <span class="identifier">sum</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">ifelse</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">x</span><span class="operator">==</span><span class="string">""</span>,<span class="number">1</span>,<span class="number">0</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="operator">==</span><span class="number">0</span><span class="paren">)</span>
<span class="identifier">select.var</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">rownames</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">var2</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">[</span><span class="identifier">var2</span><span class="operator">$</span><span class="identifier">value</span><span class="operator">==</span><span class="literal">TRUE</span><span class="paren">]</span>
<span class="identifier">train3</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">train2</span><span class="paren">[</span>,<span class="identifier">select.var</span><span class="paren">]</span>
<span class="identifier">test3</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">test2</span><span class="paren">[</span>,<span class="identifier">select.var</span><span class="paren">[</span><span class="operator">-</span><span class="identifier">length</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">select.var</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">]</span><span class="paren">]</span>
<span class="identifier">train4</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">train3</span><span class="paren">[</span>,<span class="identifier">names</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">train3</span><span class="paren">[</span><span class="operator">-</span><span class="identifier">c</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="number">1</span><span class="operator">:</span><span class="number">7</span>,<span class="identifier">length</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">train3</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">]</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">]</span>      <span class="comment"># only considering numeric variable from HAR sensor</span>
<span class="identifier">test4</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">test3</span><span class="paren">[</span>,<span class="identifier">names</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">test3</span><span class="paren">[</span><span class="operator">-</span><span class="identifier">c</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="number">1</span><span class="operator">:</span><span class="number">7</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">]</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">]</span></code></pre>
<p>Now, we have to look for correlations within numeric variables to remove multicollinearity.</p>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">correlations</span> <span class="operator">&lt;-</span> <span class="identifier">cor</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">train4</span><span class="paren">)</span>                                 <span class="comment"># finding correlations </span>
<span class="identifier">corrplot</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">correlations</span>,<span class="identifier">order</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="string">"hclust"</span>,<span class="identifier">tl.cex</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="number">.5</span><span class="paren">)</span>         <span class="comment"># plotting correlation matrix of variables</span></code></pre>

<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">highCorr</span> <span class="operator">&lt;-</span> <span class="identifier">findCorrelation</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">correlations</span>, <span class="identifier">cutoff</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="number">.75</span><span class="paren">)</span>     <span class="comment"># finding variables with high correlation</span>
<span class="identifier">predictor</span> <span class="operator">&lt;-</span> <span class="identifier">train4</span><span class="paren">[</span>, <span class="operator">-</span><span class="identifier">highCorr</span><span class="paren">]</span>                            <span class="comment"># dataframe of train predictors</span>
<span class="identifier">filtered.test4</span> <span class="operator">&lt;-</span> <span class="identifier">test4</span><span class="paren">[</span>, <span class="operator">-</span><span class="identifier">highCorr</span><span class="paren">]</span>                        <span class="comment"># dataframe of test predictors</span>
<span class="identifier">classe</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">train3</span><span class="operator">$</span><span class="identifier">classe</span>                                       <span class="comment"># target variable</span>
<span class="identifier">trainData</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span><span class="identifier">cbind</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">classe</span>,<span class="identifier">predictor</span><span class="paren">)</span>                          <span class="comment"># training dataset ready for prediction</span></code></pre>
<p>Now, we have variables which are good for prediction.</p>
</div>
<div id="random-forest-algorithm" class="section level4">
<h4>Random Forest Algorithm</h4>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">rfModel</span> <span class="operator">&lt;-</span> <span class="identifier">randomForest</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">classe</span> <span class="operator">~</span> .,<span class="identifier">data</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="identifier">trainData</span>,<span class="identifier">importance</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="literal">TRUE</span>,<span class="identifier">ntrees</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="number">10</span><span class="paren">)</span>
<span class="identifier">print</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">rfModel</span><span class="paren">)</span>                                   <span class="comment"># Confusion Matrix showing the accuracy</span></code></pre>
<pre><code>## 
## Call:
##  randomForest(formula = classe ~ ., data = trainData, importance = TRUE,      ntrees = 10) 
##                Type of random forest: classification
##                      Number of trees: 500
## No. of variables tried at each split: 5
## 
##         OOB estimate of  error rate: 0.42%
## Confusion matrix:
##      A    B    C    D    E class.error
## A 5577    2    0    0    1   0.0005376
## B   10 3781    5    0    1   0.0042139
## C    0   17 3392   13    0   0.0087668
## D    0    0   27 3186    3   0.0093284
## E    0    0    0    4 3603   0.0011090</code></pre>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">par</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">mar</span><span class="operator">=</span><span class="identifier">c</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="number">3</span>,<span class="number">4</span>,<span class="number">4</span>,<span class="number">4</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">)</span>

<h4>Saving the output for Course Project: Submission</h4>
<pre class="r"><code class="r"><span class="identifier">answers</span><span class="operator">&lt;-</span> <span class="identifier">as.vector</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">out.test</span><span class="paren">)</span>

<span class="identifier">pml_write_files</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="keyword">function</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">x</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">{</span>
  <span class="identifier">n</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="identifier">length</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">x</span><span class="paren">)</span>
  <span class="keyword">for</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">i</span> <span class="keyword">in</span> <span class="number">1</span><span class="operator">:</span><span class="identifier">n</span><span class="paren">)</span><span class="paren">{</span>
    <span class="identifier">filename</span> <span class="operator">=</span> <span class="identifier">paste0</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="string">"problem_id_"</span>,<span class="identifier">i</span>,<span class="string">".txt"</span><span class="paren">)</span>
    <span class="identifier">write.table</span><span class="paren">(</span><span class="identifier">x</span><span class="paren">[</span><span class="identifier">i</span><span class="paren">]</span>,<span class="identifier">file</span><span class="operator">=</span><span class="identifier">filename</span>,<span class="identifier">quote</span><span class="operator">=</span><span class="literal">FALSE</span>,<span class="identifier">row.names</span><span class="operator">=</span><span class="literal">FALSE</span>,<span class="identifier">col.names</span><span class="operator">=</span><span class="literal">FALSE</span><span class="paren">)</span>
  <span class="paren">}</span>
<span class="paren">}</span>
